فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات. "ما هو؟" قَدَّمَ الجنس على الخاصَّة والعَرَض العام؛ لأنَّهما خارجان عن الماهية، والجنس جُزْءٌ لها. وقوله: (ما هو؟) يخرج الفصول البعيدة، وسائر الخواص، ما عدا خواص الأنواع، فإنَّ شيئاً منها لا يُقالُ في جوابِ ما هو؟. وقوله: والجنس جزء لها أي: فهو داخل فيها، وهما خارجان عنها، والداخل مُقدَّم على الخارج. ثم بيان أن الجنس يصدق عليه حين كونه مقولاً على مختلفين أنه مقول على متفقين أعني الحصص، فلا بد من قيد الحيثية. وظهر من هذا قول أبي الفتح: إن كل كلّي له أفراد في نفس الأمر، فهو نوع حقيقي بالقياس إلى حصصه المضافة إلى تلك الأفراد، وإن كان بالقياس إلى تلك الأفراد واحداً من الأقسام الباقية. مثلاً: الحيوان جنس بالقياس إلى الأفراد الإنسانية أو الفرسية، ونوع بالقياس إلى حصصه المضافة إليها. وحينئذ فلا بد من اعتبار قيد الحيثية في تعاريفها احترازاً عن مادة الاجتماع. وقيل: كون الجنس جزءاً للماهية ومقولاً عليها غير معقول؛ لأن الجزء يتقدم على الكل في الوجودين، والمحمول متحد الوجود بالموضوع في الخارج. قلنا: ليس المراد أن الخبر محمول من حيث إنه جزء يكون محمولاً، بل المراد أن معروض الجزئية هو معروض المحمولية. مثلاً: الحيوان المأخوذ بشرط أن يدخل فيه الناطق نوع، وبشرط أن لا يدخل فيه جزء، والمأخوذ بحيث يمكن أن تعرض له الجزئية والنوعية. وقدَّم الجنس على الفصل لاحتياجنا في معرفة الفصل القريب والبعيد إلى الجنس. وعلى النوع لتوقف معرفة قسم من النوع وهو النوع الإضافي على الجنس. وترك من تعريف الجنس وسائر الكليات لفظ "الكلِّي"؛ لأن المقول على الكثرة مغن عنه.
Chapter: On the principles of concepts. "What is it?" He gave priority to genus over specific difference and universal accident because both are external to the quiddity, while genus is a part of it. And his saying: "What is it?" excludes remote differentiae and all properties except the properties of species, for none of them is said in answer to "What is it?". And his saying: "Genus is a part of it" means it is internal to it, while the two are external, and the internal is given priority over the external. Then an explanation that genus, when it is predicated of different things, is also predicated of agreeing things, namely the individual cases, so a qualification of aspect is necessary. From this emerges the saying of Abu al-Fath: Every universal that has individuals in reality is a true species relative to its sub-parts added to those individuals, even if relative to those individuals it is one of the remaining divisions. For example: animal is a genus relative to human or horse individuals, and a species relative to its sub-parts added to them. Therefore, it is necessary to consider the qualification of aspect in their definitions to avoid the material of commonality. It is said: The fact that genus is part of the quiddity and predicated upon it is unintelligible because the part precedes the whole in both existences, while the predicate is united in existence with the subject in the external. We say: The intention is not that the predicate, from the aspect that it is a part, is predicated; rather the intention is that the substrate of part-hood is the same as the substrate of predicate-hood. For example: animal taken with the condition that rational enters into it is a species, and taken with the condition that rational does not enter into it is a part, and taken in a way that allows part-hood and species-hood to befall it. And he gave priority to genus over differentia because we need the genus to know the proximate and remote differentiae. And over species because the knowledge of a type of species, namely the relative species, depends on the genus. And he omitted from the definition of genus and all the universal the word "universal" because "predicated of many" suffices for it.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and explanatory passage from a commentary on Tahzeeb al-Mantiq. It begins with the chapter heading 'On the principles of concepts' and immediately addresses the question 'What is it?' (ma huwa) which is the standard question for definitions of quiddities. The author states that genus (jins) is given priority over specific difference (fasl) and universal accident ('arad 'amm) in the order of definition because genus is a part (juz') of the quiddity (mahiyya), while the other two are external to it. This is a key logical principle: the internal (al-dakhil) is prior to the external (al-kharij). The commentator explains that the phrase 'What is it?' when used in definition excludes remote differentiae (fusul ba'ida) and all properties (khawas) except those that are actual species-specific properties, since these are not given in answer to 'What is it?' but rather to 'What kind of thing is it?' or similar. Next, the author clarifies that genus is predicated of both different things (e.g., animal predicated of human and horse) and also of agreeing things (i.e., the individual instances). This dual predication necessitates adding a qualification (qayd al-haythiyya) to avoid equivocation. The passage then cites Abu al-Fath's principle: any universal that has real individuals is a true species relative to its own subparts (e.g., animal is a species relative to the sub-category 'rational animal'? Actually, the example: animal is a genus relative to human and horse individuals, but a species relative to its sub-parts like 'sentient animal'? The text says 'animal is a genus relative to human or horse individuals, and a species relative to its sub-parts added to them.' This illustrates the relative nature of genus and species depending on perspective. The author then addresses an objection: how can genus be both a part of the quiddity and predicated of it, since a part precedes the whole in existence (mental and external) while a predicate is united with its subject in external existence? The response distinguishes that it is not the genus qua part that is predicated, but rather the same meaning (ma'na) that can be considered as a part (under one condition) or as a whole/species (under another). The example of 'animal' is given: if taken with the condition that 'rational' enters into it, it is a species; if with the condition that 'rational' does not enter, it is a part; and if taken without condition, it can be considered either. Thus, the substrate of part-hood and of predicate-hood are the same. Finally, the passage gives reasons for prioritizing genus over specific difference (fasl): we need genus to know both proximate and remote differentiae (e.g., to know that 'rational' is the proximate differentia of human, we first know the genus 'animal'). Genus is also prior to species because a certain kind of species—the relative species (naw' idafi)—is defined by genus (e.g., the definition of 'animal' as a species relative to 'living body' includes its genus 'body'). The author also notes that the word 'kulli' (universal) is omitted from the definition of genus and other universals because the phrase 'predicated of many' (al-maqul 'ala al-kathra) already conveys the meaning of universality succinctly.

Checkpoint
How does the passage resolve the objection that genus cannot be both a part of the quiddity and predicated of it?
A) By denying that genus is a part.
B) By stating that the predicate is not considered as a part when it is predicated.
C) By changing the definition of genus.
D) By saying the objection is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Genus can be both a part of the quiddity and a predicate because predication considers the meaning without the condition of part-hood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition of 'sword' as 'a weapon used for cutting'. The genus 'weapon' is a part of the quiddity of sword. Explain how the objection that a part cannot be predicated is resolved using the condition of part-hood vs. predication.
?
In fiqh, 'marriage' is defined as 'a contract that permits intimacy'. The genus 'contract' is a part of the definition. Reconstruct the objection and provide the resolution in your own words.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
12 min
Refining the Definition of Universal
Commentators refine the definition of 'universal'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'maqul ala kathirin' must be interpreted as potentially predicable, using the example of the concept of the Necessary (al-wajib) to defend the definition.

Core Idea
The universal is not what is actually predicated, but what is fit to be predicated.

This lesson explores a key refinement in the definition of 'universal' (kulli). The commentators analyze whether 'maqul ala kathirin' (predicable of many) means actual predication or potential. The correct interpretation is crucial to include concepts like the Necessary (al-wajib) and hypothetical universals, which have no multiple actual individuals yet are universal. We will walk through the logical steps that lead to this conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
In the passage, the term being defined is 'kulli' (universal). The proposed definition is 'maqul ala kathirin' (predicable of many). Note that some commentators argue whether the word 'kulli' is redundant or necessary.
Al-Sayyid says the two terms have the same concept, but 'kulli' indicates it implicitly while 'maqul ala kathirin' indicates it explicitly.
2
Distinguish implicit vs explicit definition
Al-Sayyid states that 'kulli' and 'maqul ala kathirin' are identical in meaning, but differ in explicitness. This shows that the definition can be expressed in two ways, but the core concept is the same.
3
Understand potential vs actual predication
The passage argues that 'maqul' in the definition does not mean 'actually predicated' (bi al-fi'l), but 'fit to be predicated' (salih). If actual predication were required, then universals with no actual individuals (like hypothetical universals) or only one individual (like the Necessary) would be excluded. Since these are still considered universals, the definition must mean potential.
This is the central logical move: preferring potential over actual protects the universality of concepts like the Necessary.
4
Analyze al-Dawwani's first objection
Al-Dawwani objects that if 'maqul' is taken as 'possible to be predicated', then hypothetical universals would enter the definition. The rebuttal distinguishes between considering them as existing and mutually exclusive (in which case they cannot be truly predicated of others) and disregarding that (in which case they are still fit). The latter is harmless.
The key is to note that hypothetical universals are indeed fit to be predicated, even if not actually. The objection only fails if one insists on actual predication.
5
Evaluate the second objection and its rebuttal
Al-Dawwani also objects that universals without individuals are not genera. The rebuttal states that al-Sayyid's concern is that they would be excluded from all five universals, not just genus, which is unacceptable because the concept of the Necessary is clearly a universal. Hence, the definition must include them.
This shows that the definition of universal must be broad enough to cover all types of universals, including those with no actual individuals.

الدسوقي
وقِيلَ: لأنَّ المقول معناه: الصَّالحُ لِلمَقُولِيَّةِ بحسب نفس الأمر؛ أي: لا بحسب الفرض، وهو أخصُّ مِنَ الكُلِّيِّ، ويلزمُ مِن وجودِ الأخصِّ وجودُ الأعم. وقد ذكر المصنِّفُ في شرحِ التَّلخيص : أنَّ الَّذِي يُقالُ ويُحملُ؛ إنّما هو الكُلِّي لا الجزئي، ونحو هذا زيدٌ ; مُؤوَّلٌ بهذا مُسمَّى بزيد، وحيثُ كانَ الَّذي يُحملُ،
العطار
ومثله في حاشية الجلالِ ، فإِنَّهُ قالَ : حَذْفُ لفظ (الكُلِّيِّ) لا لإغناء لفظ المقول على الكثرة عنه ؛ إذ الكُلِّي جنس له، وذِكْرُ الجنس واجبُ في التَّعريفاتِ التَّامَّةِ ا.هـ.، والحقُّ مَا قالَهُ الشَّارح، ويؤيده قولُ السَّيِّدِ : إِنَّ مَفهومَ الكُلِّيّ هو مفهوم المقول على كثيرين بِعِينِهِ، إلا أنَّ لفظ (الكُلِّيّ) يدلُّ عليهِ إجمالاً، ولفظ (المقول على كثيرين) يدلُّ عليهِ تَفصيلاً، لا يُقالُ: مَفهومُ الكُلِّيّ هُوَ الصَّالِحُ لِأَنْ يُقال بالفرضِ على كثيرين، ومفهوم المقول على كثيرين ما كانَ مَقولاً على كثيرين بالفعل، فَلَا يُغني عنه ؛ لأنَّ دَلالةَ المقولِ بالفعل على الصَّالِحِ لِأَنْ يُقالَ على كَثيرين التزام، ودلالة الالتزام ليسَتْ مُعتبرةً في التّعريفات؛ لأنَّا نَقولُ : لم يرد بالمقول على كثيرين في تعريف الكُلِّيَّاتِ إلَّا الصَّالحُ لِأَنْ يقال على كثيرين؛ إذْ لَوْ أُريدَ بِهِ المقولُ بالفعل ؛ يخرج عن تعريف الكُلِّيَّاتِ مفهومات كُلِّيَّةٌ ليس لها أفراد موجودة في الخارج ولا في الذهن؛ سواءٌ لم يكنْ لَهَا أفراد أصلاً كَالكُلِّيَّاتِ الفرضية، أو كان لها فرد واحد في الخارج والذهن بناءً على برهان امتناع تعدُّدِ الواجب خارجاً وذهناً، فإنَّها لا تكونُ مقولة بالفعل ؛ بل بالصلاحية، فيكون المقولُ على كثيرين بمعنى الكُلِّيّ. ا.هـ. وأما ما أوردَهُ علَيهِ الدَّوَّانِيُّ أولاً بأنَّ الكُلِّيَّ هو الذي يُمكنُ فرضُ الشَّركةِ فيهِ؛ أي : فرضُ مَقوليَّتِهِ على كَثيرينَ ولَوْ حمل المقولُ في التَّعريف على ما يمكنُ فرضُ مقوليَّتِهِ؛ لَدَخَلَ في التَّعريف الكُلِّيَّاتُ الفرضيَّةُ بالنسبة إلى الحقائق الموجودة، إذْ يمكنُ فرضُ مَقوليّتها عليها ، بل الكُلِّيَّات المتباينة بالنسبة إلى الماهية مطلقاً، وأما ثانياً ; فلأنَّ الكُلِّيَّات التى ليسَتْ لَهَا أفراد أصلاً ليسَتْ أجناساً لشيءٍ، فَلا بأسَ بخروجها، ومن ههنا؛ ينقدحُ أنَّ المنحصر في الخمس هو الكُلِّيَّاتُ الَّتي لَهَا أفراد
فالمقولُ على الكثرة جنس يشمّلُ الكُلِّيَّات.
الدسوقي
ويقال: إنَّما هو الكُلِّي؛ صارَ الجزئي خارجاً بقوله : (المقول)، وحينئذ؛ فَلا حاجة لكونه يقول : الكُلّي المقول ... إلخ .
(قَوْلُهُ : عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ) أي : على ذي الكثرة، ولم يقل على الكثيرين؛ لأنه أخصُّ ; لأنَّ الكثيرين جمعُ العقلاء، مع أنَّه ليس بلازم أن تكون الأفراد عقلاء. (قَوْلُهُ : فَالمَقُوْلُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ جِنْسٌ إِنَّما جعلَ المجموع جنساً، ولم يجعل المقول جنساً، وعلى الكثرة فصلاً مخرجاً للجزئي؛ لأنَّ الجزئي لا يحملُ بأن تقول : هذا زيد .
العطار
أنَّ أَمَّا عَنِ الأَوَّلِ ; فَلِأَنَّهُ إِنْ أَرادَ أَنَّهُ يدخلُ فيها مِنْ حيث إنّها حقائق موجودةٌ ومُباينةٌ ; فَممنوع؛ إذْ لا يمكنُ فرضُ صدقها عليها ، وإن أراد أنَّهُ يدخلُ فيها مع قطعِ النَّظَرِ عَنْ صدق الوجودِ عليها، وكونها مُباينةً ; فَمُسلَّم ولا ضرر في ذلك، وأَمَّا عَن الثَّاني ; فَلِأَنَّ مَقصودَ السَّيِّدِ أَنَّهُ يلزمُ خروجُهَا عَنِ الكُلِّيَّاتِ الخمسِ؛ لَا خروجها عَنِ الجنس فقط، ولا شَكٌّ أنَّ القول بأنَّ مفهوم الواجب ليس شيئاً منها؛ باطل، على عدم الأفرادِ في نفس الأمرِ لا يُنافي كونَها أجناساً باعتبار إمكان الفرض، وليتَ شعري أنَّها إذا لم تكن داخلةٌ في الكُلْيَّاتِ الخمس ; فَما فائدة إدراجها في تعريف الكُلّيّ ا.هـ. ، وأمَّا زيادة المحشّي قوله : أو بالإمكان; بعد قولِ السَّيِّدِ : إِنَّ المراد بِهِ المقوليَّةُ بالفعل; فَزيادةٌ مُضِرَّةٌ كما لا يخفى; تَأَمَّلْ . (قَوْلُهُ : فَالمَقَوْلُ عَلَى الْكَثْرَةِ جِنْسٌ ) أي : هذا المجموع كما يدلُّ عليه كلامه؛ لأنَّهُ أُقِيمَ مَقامَ الكُلِّي ولم يُجعَل المقول جنساً ، وَقَولُهُ: (على الكثرة) فصلاً لإخراج الجزئي ; فإنَّهُ مقول، لكن على الواحدِ; للخلافِ في صحة حمل الجزئي ; فإِنَّ السَّيِّدَ مَنَعَهُ، قال في حاشية شرح المطالع كونُ الشَّخْصِ محمولاً على شيءٍ حَمْلاً إيجابيا ; إنَّما هو بحسب الظاهرِ ; لأنَّ الجزئي الحقيقي من حيثُ هو جزئي حقيقي ; لا يحمل على نفسِهِ لعدم التغايرِ، وَلَا على غيرِهِ; لأنَّهُ الهوية المتأصلَةُ، فلا يصدقُ
CHAPTER: On the Principles of Concepts. al-Dasuqi: And it was said: Because 'maqul' (predicable) means: that which is fit for predication according to the actual state of affairs; i.e., not according to assumption, and it is more specific than the universal, and from the existence of the more specific follows the existence of the more general. And the author mentioned in Sharh al-Talkhis that what is said and predicated is only the universal, not the particular, and something like 'this Zayd' is interpreted as meaning this named 'Zayd', and when it is what is predicated... al-Attar: And similar is in Hashiyat al-Jalal, for he said: The omission of the word 'universal' is not because the word 'maqul 'ala al-kathrah' suffices for it; for the universal is a genus for it, and the mention of the genus is necessary in complete definitions. End. And the truth is what the commentator said, and it is supported by the statement of al-Sayyid: Indeed, the concept of the universal is precisely the concept of that which is predicated of many, except that the word 'universal' indicates it implicitly, and the word 'predicated of many' indicates it explicitly. It cannot be said: The concept of the universal is that which is fit to be said by assumption of many, and the concept of 'predicated of many' is what is actually predicated of many, so it does not suffice for it; because the indication of what is actually predicated of that which is fit to be said of many is a concomitant indication, and concomitant indication is not considered in definitions; because we say: By 'predicated of many' in the definition of universals is meant only that which is fit to be said of many; for if what is actually predicated were intended, then universal concepts that have no individuals existing externally or mentally would be excluded from the definition of universals; whether they have no individuals at all, like hypothetical universals, or they have only one individual externally and mentally, based on the proof of the impossibility of multiplicity of the Necessary in externals and mind, for they are not actually predicated, but only potentially, so 'predicated of many' has the meaning of universal. End. As for what al-Dawwani objected to him: first, that the universal is that which can have participation assumed in it, i.e., assumption of its being predicated of many; if the 'maqul' in the definition is taken as that which can have its predication assumed, then hypothetical universals enter the definition relative to existing realities, since their predication on them can be assumed, indeed mutually exclusive universals relative to the quiddity absolutely. And second, because universals that have no individuals at all are not genera of anything, so there is no harm in their exclusion. From here it becomes apparent that what is confined to the five is the universals that have individuals. So 'al-maqul 'ala al-kathrah' is a genus that includes universals. al-Dasuqi: And it is said: It is only the universal; the particular is excluded by his saying 'al-maqul'; so then, there is no need for him to say 'the universal, the predicable...' etc. (His saying: 'ala al-kathrah' i.e., upon that which has multiplicity; he did not say 'upon many' because it is more specific, since 'many' is the plural of rational beings, while it is not necessary that the individuals be rational. (His saying: 'fa al-maqul 'ala al-kathrah' is a genus; he made the composite a genus, and did not make 'al-maqul' a genus, and 'ala al-kathrah' a differentia to exclude the particular, because the particular is not predicated such that you say 'this is Zayd'. al-Attar: As for the first objection, it is because if he means that it enters into them insofar as they are existing and mutually exclusive realities, it is denied, for it is impossible to assume their truth about them; and if he means that it enters into them while disregarding the truth of existence upon them and their being mutually exclusive, it is granted and there is no harm in that. As for the second, because al-Sayyid's intention is that their exclusion from the five universals necessarily follows, not their exclusion from genus alone; and there is no doubt that the statement that the concept of the Necessary is not one of them is false; the lack of individuals in actual reality does not negate their being genera from the perspective of possibility of assumption. And I wish I knew, if they are not included in the five universals, then what is the benefit of including them in the definition of universal? End. As for the addition of the commentator (al-muhashshi) saying 'or by possibility' after al-Sayyid's statement that what is intended is actual predication, it is a harmful addition, as is clear; ponder. (His saying: 'fa al-maqul 'ala al-kathrah' is a genus) i.e., this composite, as his speech indicates, because it was put in place of the universal and 'al-maqul' was not made a genus, and his saying 'ala al-kathrah' is a differentia to exclude the particular, for it is predicable, but of the one; due to disagreement about the validity of predicating the particular; for al-Sayyid denied it. He said in Hashiyat Sharh al-Matali': The predication of a person of something as positive predication is only apparent, because the true particular, insofar as it is a true particular, is not predicated of itself due to lack of difference, nor of another, because it is the essence itself, so it is not true.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the definition of 'universal' (kulli) as 'that which is predicable of many' (maqul 'ala kathirin). It opens with a discussion of the precision of the term 'maqul' in definitions. The author notes that 'maqul' means that which is fit for predication according to the actual state of affairs (bi hasab nafs al-amr), not merely by assumption, and that this meaning is more specific than 'kulli' because it adds the idea of actual fitness. However, the concept of 'kulli' is more general. The commentator then cites al-Sayyid al-Jurjani's view that the two terms are identical in concept but differ in explicitness: 'kulli' indicates implicitly, while 'maqul ala kathirin' indicates explicitly. The passage defends the use of 'maqul ala kathirin' in definitions by arguing that it means potentially (salih) not actually (bi al-fi'l), because if actual predication were required, universals with no actual individuals (e.g., hypothetical universals or the concept of the Necessary being with only one individual) would be excluded. This is unacceptable because such universals are still considered universals (they are fit to be predicated of many in principle). The passage then addresses objections from al-Dawwani: first, that if 'maqul' is taken as 'possible to be predicated', then hypothetical universals would enter the definition, and second, that universals without individuals need not be considered genera. The commentator rebuts the first objection by distinguishing between considering them as existing and mutually exclusive vs. disregarding that; only in the latter case do they enter, and that is harmless. For the second, he argues that al-Sayyid's point is that such universals would be excluded from the five universals altogether, not just from genus, which is problematic because the concept of the Necessary is clearly a universal. The passage concludes with a discussion of why 'maqul ala al-kathrah' is taken as a genus and 'ala al-kathrah' as a differentia to exclude the particular, and clarifies that the particular is not truly predicable except apparently, according to al-Sayyid. All examples and arguments are grounded in the Islamic logical tradition, focusing on the technical definition of universal and its implications for the five universals (al-kulliyyat al-khams).

المقول على كثيرين
المقولية
الكليات الخمس
الكليات الفرضية

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must 'maqul ala kathirin' in the definition of the universal be interpreted as meaning 'fit to be predicated' (salih) rather than 'actually predicated' (bi al-fi'l)?
A) Because the Arabic language requires it.
B) Because otherwise, universals like the concept of the Necessary (al-wajib) would be excluded as they have only one individual.
C) Because al-Dawwani objected to the definition.

Key Takeaway
The definition of universal relies on potential rather than actual predication to include all genuine universals, especially those with no or single individuals.

Analyzing the Definition of Genus: Objections and Refinements
Author defines genus, responds to an objection, and engages with later critiques.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to dissect the definition of genus, identify its two restrictions, and explain how the aspectual restriction (hathiyya) resolves an objection.

Core Idea
Genus is predicated of many differing realities, but predication of consistent realities is explained by a different aspect.

This passage presents the definition of genus and then engages with a critical objection that challenges the definition's exclusivity. The response introduces the concept of 'aspectual restriction' (hathiyya), a key tool for handling apparent counterexamples. Understanding this debate strengthens your ability to evaluate definitions in Islamic logic and its applied sciences.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition
From the text, genus is defined as 'predicated of many consistent in reality in answer to what is it?' Note the two restrictions: 'consistent in reality' and 'in answer to what is it?'.
Though the text says 'consistent in reality', the later discussion shows that genus is actually of differing realities; the restriction is qualified.
2
Identify the objection
The objector says: genus may be said of individuals consistent in reality, e.g., 'animal' for Zayd, Bakr, Amr (all human) when no other animal is present. This violates the first restriction.
3
Analyze the answer
The author responds that the restriction 'consistent in reality' is considered from a specific aspect (haythu). Genus is predicated of such individuals not because they are consistent, but because of a participant that differs in reality (e.g., the horse).
The aspectual restriction saves the definition.
4
Examine the later refinements
Abd al-Hakim objects that a single restriction is insufficient because genus also applies to its portions (hisas) which are consistent. Al-Dawwani offers an alternative: restrict to essential predication. The genus is essentially predicated of differing realities, and its predication of consistent realities is by concomitance.

(قَوْلُهُ : فِي جَوَابِ) خرجَ العَرَضُ العام ، وقولُهُ : (ما هو؟) خرجَ الفصلُ القريب كَناطق، والخاصَّة ؛ أي : خاصَّةُ النَّوعِ كَـ: (الضَّاحك)، فَالفصلُ القريب، وخاصَّةً النّوع ؛ كلٌّ منهما، وإنْ كانَ يُقالُ على الأفرادِ الكثيرة المتفقة في الحقيقة؛ لكن في جواب «أي»، وبعبارة قوله: (في جواب ما هو؟) خرج الفصل، والخاصة، والعَرَضُ العالم بالنسبة إلى جنس الماهية ، فإنَّ الجنس مقول ومحمول على الفصل، كالنَّاطِقِ، فيُقالُ : النَّاطِقُ حيوان، وعلى الخاصَّةِ : الضاحك)، فيُقالُ: الضَّاحك كَـ: حيوان، وعلى العَرَضِ العام : ( الماشي) . فيُقالُ : الماشي حيوان لكن لا في جواب ما هو ؟ ؛ إذ ليس الحيوان تمام المشتركِ، وَلَا ذاتيا لهذهِ الثَّلاثة . بالنسبة إلى جنس الماهيَّةِ ؛ أي: وأمَّا بالنسبة إلى أجناسها الداخلة فيها فأنواع إضافية . وقولِي فيها ؛ فأنواع إضافية . كقولنا : ما زيدٌ وعَمْرُو وهذا الفرس ؛ فَلَا بُدَّ مِن قيدٍ فقط ليخرج الجنس ؛ هذا كلامه، وقال عبد الحكيم : إِنَّ التَّقييدَ بِقَيدٍ فقط ؛ فاسد؛ لأنَّه يُخرجُ الجنس بالقياس إلى حِصَصِهِ، واختار في الجوابِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ قَبيلِ تَعليقِ الحُكم بالمشتقّ المؤذنِ بالعليَّةِ ؛ أي: الكثرة المتفقة الحقيقة أي : مِن أجل كَونِهِم مُتَّفقينَ بِالحقيقةِ، فَعِلَّهُ المقولية هي أنَّ تلكَ الكثرة مُتفقةُ الحقيقة .ا.هـ. والحصَّةُ هِيَ الكُلّي المقيَّدُ بِقَيْدٍ جزئي أو كُلّيّ، والقيد خارج ، وكُلُّ كُلّيّ بِالقياس إلى حِصَصِهِ؛ نوع حقيقي والحِصَصُ أفراد اعتباريَّةٌ ، وَوَجهُ خروج الجنس بالقياس إلى حِصَصِهِ؛ أَنَّ تِلكَ الحِصَّصَ أفراد لَهُ، ومَقُوليِّتُهُ عليها مَقُوليَّةُ النَّوع ، فَهُوَ مِنْ هذهِ الحيثيَّةِ مَقولٌ على الكثرةِ المُتَّفقةِ الحقيقةِ، فَلَو قُيْدَ بِقيدٍ فقط ؛ صدقَ أنَّ الجنس كالحيوان مثلاً ؛ مقول على هذه الحصص فقط؛ لا على غيرِهَا، ومَعلومٌ أَنَّهُ يُقالُ على أفرادِهِ الأُخرِ كَالإنسانِ والفرس ؛ مِنْ حيثُ كونُهُمَا مُختَلِفي الحقيقةِ؛ تَأَمَّلْ، وأجابَ الدَّوَّانِيُّ بجواب آخر، وهوَ : تقييد المقوليَّةِ بالذَّاتِ والمقول في الصُّورة المذكورة؛ مقولةٌ بالذَّاتِ على الأمور المختلفة الحقيقة، وأمَّا قَولُهُ على المتَّفقةِ الواقعة معها ؛ فَقَوْلُ والمقولُ مَحمولٌ على مَا هوَ مَقولٌ بِالذَّاتِ ؛ لأنَّ المتبادر مِنَ المقول على بِالتَّبِعِ،
Chapter: On the principles of concepts [that are] consistent in reality in answer to 'what is it?'. So that which is predicated of many is genus as we mentioned, and by the restriction 'consistent in reality' the genus is excluded, and by his statement 'in answer to what is it?' the rest of the universals are excluded. (His statement: 'consistent in reality' excludes the genus, its specific property like 'walking', and the remote differentia like 'sensitive', and each of these three, although it is said of many individuals, but they are different in reality. If you say: indeed genus may be said of individuals consistent in reality, like: what is Zayd, Bakr, Amr, and the horse? So it is valid to say in answer: animal, and then the definition of the species is not exclusive. The answer: that what is meant by his statement 'consistent in reality' is: from the aspect that they are consistent, so the aspectual restriction is considered in the definition. As for the predication of genus in the mentioned example of Zayd, Amr, and Bakr, it is not from the aspect of their consistency in reality, but from the aspect of the existence of a participant with them in the question that differs from them in reality, which is the horse. (His statement: 'and by the restriction of consistent in reality') the idafa is for clarification. (His statement: 'and by his statement: in answer to what is it? ... etc.') It is better that he say: and in answer the accidental general is excluded. And his statement 'what is it?' excludes the specific property and the differentia as previously. (His statement: 'in answer') excludes the accidental general, and his statement 'what is it?' excludes the proximate differentia like 'rational', and the specific property; i.e., the specific property of the species like 'laughing', so the proximate differentia and the specific property of the species; each of them, although said of many individuals consistent in reality, but in answer to 'which one?', and in the expression of his statement: (in answer to what is it?) excludes the differentia, the specific property, and the accidental general with respect to the genus of the quiddity, for the genus is predicated and predicated of the differentia, like 'rational', so it is said: the rational is an animal, and of the specific property: 'the laughing', so it is said: the laughing is like an animal, and of the accidental general: 'the walking'. So it is said: the walking is an animal but not in answer to 'what is it?' because animal is not the complete shared [genus] nor essential to these three. With respect to the genus of the quiddity; i.e., and with respect to the genera internal to them, they are relative species. And my statement in them: they are relative species. Like our saying: what is Zayd, Amr, and this horse? So a single restriction is necessary to exclude the genus; this is his statement. And Abd al-Hakim said: indeed the single restriction is corrupt because it excludes the genus with respect to its portions (hisas). And he chose in the answer that it is of the type of suspending the ruling on the derived [word] indicating causation; i.e., the many consistent in reality means: because they are consistent in reality, so the cause of predication is that that many is consistent in reality. End. And the portion (hissa) is the universal restricted by a particular or universal restriction, and the restriction is external, and every universal with respect to its portions is a true species, and the portions are notional individuals. And the way of exclusion of the genus with respect to its portions is that those portions are individuals of it, and its predication upon them is predication of the species, so it is from this aspect predicated of the many consistent in reality. So if it were restricted by a single restriction, it would be true that the genus like animal for example is predicated of these portions only, not of others, and it is known that it is said of its other individuals like human and horse from the aspect of their being different in reality; reflect. And al-Dawwani answered with another answer, which is: restricting the predication to essential, and the predicated in the mentioned form is essentially predicated of matters different in reality, and as for his statement 'on the consistent' occurring with them, it is a predication and the predicated is predicated of what is essentially predicated, because the understood from the predicated on... by way of concomitance.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of genus (jins), one of the five universals. The author begins by stating the definition: 'that which is predicated of many consistent in reality in answer to 'what is it?''. Then he explains that the restriction 'consistent in reality' excludes the genus, its specific property, and the remote differentia, because although each is predicated of many, those many are different in reality. An objection is raised: the genus (e.g., 'animal') can be predicated of individuals that are consistent in reality (e.g., Zayd, Bakr, Amr) when no animal of different kind is present, so the definition would not be exclusive (it would also apply to species). The answer is that the consistency is considered from a certain aspect: the genus is predicated of those individuals not because they are consistent in reality, but because there is a participant in the question that differs in reality (the horse). So the restriction is aspectual (hathiyya). The commentary then clarifies the second restriction 'in answer to what is it?' It excludes the accidental general (which is answered with 'which one?'), the proximate differentia, and the specific property. For example, 'animal' can be predicated of 'rational', 'laughing', and 'walking', but not in answer to 'what is it?' because animal is not the complete genus for those. The discussion then turns to whether a single restriction is sufficient. Abd al-Hakim criticizes that a single restriction would exclude the genus when considered relative to its portions (hisas), which are individuals of the genus but consistent in reality (e.g., human and horse are portions of animal). He suggests a causal interpretation: the phrase 'consistent in reality' means 'because they are consistent', so the predication's cause is consistency. Al-Dawwani offers another solution: restrict predication to essential predication; the genus is essentially predicated of things different in reality, and its predication of the consistent occurs by way of concomitance.

D) The distinction between essential and accidental predication

Key Takeaway
Genus is essentially predicated of many differing realities; its apparent predication of consistent realities is explained by an aspectual restriction, a concept crucial for refining definitions in Islamic logic.

Critiquing Claims of Simplicity: The Case of the Point
Commentators debate the point's simplicity and its definition as end of line.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the conditional syllogism used in the critique of the point's simplicity and evaluate its validity by distinguishing external and intellectual simplicity.

Core Idea
Simplicity can be external or intellectual; confusing them leads to invalid arguments about definition.

This passage from the logic commentary tradition examines the definition of the point (nuqta) as the end of a line and whether it is simple (basita). The commentators use a conditional syllogism to argue that the point has no genus, but they also critique that argument. By analyzing this passage, you will learn how to deconstruct such arguments and identify ambiguities in key terms.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish external vs intellectual simplicity
Identify in Dasuqi's comment the two senses of 'simple': external (ontological) simplicity meaning no parts in existence, and intellectual (conceptual) simplicity meaning no parts in definition. The point is externally simple but intellectually composite because its definition includes 'end' and 'line'.
This distinction is crucial for evaluating the syllogism.
2
Reconstruct the conditional syllogism
Attar presents a 'folded syllogism'. Unfold it: If the point had a genus, it would not be simple (Premise 1). The point is simple (Premise 2, by hypothesis). Therefore, the point has no genus (Conclusion). This is modus tollens.
The syllogism is valid in form, but its premises are contested.
3
Identify the hidden premise
The syllogism assumes that 'simple' means 'not having a genus' in the intellectual sense. But the point's definition shows it has intellectual parts (end and line), so it is not intellectually simple. Thus, the second premise is false if simple is taken intellectually.
The ambiguity of 'simple' weakens the argument.
4
Evaluate the critique of al-Dawwani
Al-Dawwani claims the point is a real type (naw' haqiqi) because it has no category. The commentator shows this only proves no highest genus, not no genus at all. The point could have a specific genus, making it conceptually composite.
The critique exposes the insufficiency of the original argument.
5
Assess the overall logical strength
The passage demonstrates how logical analysis deconstructs a seemingly simple claim. The point's simplicity is upheld externally but denied intellectually. The conditional syllogism is valid but unsound due to equivocation.
This method is applicable to any theological or philosophical definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل: في مبادئ التصورات
تكون بسيطةً، هذا خُلْفٌ .
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ : هَذَا خُلْفٌ) أي : كونها غير بسيطةٍ ؛ خُلْف؛ أي : مطروح وراء الخلف؛ لكونها بسيطة .
وفيه : أَنَّهُ إنْ أرادَ بسيطةٌ خارجاً ؛ فمُسلَّم، ولكن لا يضرنَا، وإنْ أراد عقلاً ؛ فَلَا ؛ لأنَّها نهاية الخط، فهي مُركَّبةٌ مُقيَّدةٌ بكونها نهاية الخطّ ؛ أي : إِنَّهَا مُركَّبَةٌ مِن مطلقِ النّهايةِ، وَمِنْ هذا القيد، تأمل.
العطار
هي لقياس مطوي تقريره : لو اندرجت تحت جنس لم تكن بسيطة، والتّالي باطل؛ لأنَّهُ خلافُ المفروض، لا يُقالُ : مُندرجةٌ تحتَ العَرَضِ ؛ لأنَّا نقولُ : ليس هو جنساً عالياً لِمَا تحتَهُ مِنَ المقولات؛ لأنَّه ليس ذاتيا لها، قال في شرح المقاصد: المعنى مِنَ الجوهر؛ ذاتُ الشَّيء وحقيقته، فيكون ذاتيًا بِخِلافِ العَرض فإنَّ معناه ما يعرضُ للموضوع، وعروضُ الشَّيءِ لِلشَّيء إِنَّما يكونُ بعدَ تَحقُّقِ حَقيقتِهِ فَلَا يكون ذاتيًّا لِمَا تَحتَهُ مِنَ الأفراد، وإنْ جازَ أنْ يكونَ ذاتيًا لما فيها مِنَ الحِصص ؛ كالماشي لحقيقتِهِ العارضة للحيوانات ا.هـ. وفي الدَّوَّاني : النُّقطة نوع حقيقي، وليست نوعاً إضافيًا، أمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِاتّفاقِ أفرادِهَا بالحقيقة، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَلِأنَّها لا تدخل تحتَ مَقولةٍ مِنَ المقولات، وإِنْ دَخلَتْ تحت العرض؛ لكن العرض ليسَ جِنساً لِمَا تحتَهُ، أو لأنَّها بسيطةٌ ؛ أي : فَلَا تكونُ مُركَّبَةً مِنَ الجنس والفصل، فَلا تكونُ نَوعاً إضافيًا ؛ لوجوبِ اندراج النَّوع الإضافي تحتَ الجنس، وكلا الوجهين ضعيفٌ، أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِأَنَّهُ لا يدلُّ عَلى أنَّ لا جنسَ لَهَا ، بل على أن لا جنسَ لَهَا عالياً، وربَّما كانَ لَهَا جنس مفرد؛ إذ المنحصر في المقولات هو الأجناسُ العالية فقط، فجازَ أن تكونَ مُركَّبةٌ مِنَ الأجزاء العقلية المتحدة في الوجودِ الخارجي؛ كسائر الماهياتِ المركَّبةِ مِنَ الأجناس والفصول، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فَلانَّ البساطة العقلية ممنوعة، والخارجيَّة لا تُجدي نفعاً ؛ لأنَّ الجنس ليس جزءاً خارجيًا ؛ بل هوَ مِنَ الأجزاء العقلية، فجازَ أَنْ يكونَ للنّقطة جزء عقلي، وهو جنس لها
Section: On the Principles of Concepts. They are simple; this is contradictory. Dasuqi: (His saying: 'this is contradictory') i.e., that they are not simple is contradictory; i.e., cast behind because they are simple. And in it: If he means simple in external existence, it is conceded, but it does not harm us. If he means in the intellect, then not, because it is the end of the line, so it is composite, restricted by being the end of the line; i.e., it is composed of absolute end and this restriction. Ponder. Attar: It is a folded syllogism, its formulation: If it were included under a genus, it would not be simple. The consequent is false because it contradicts the hypothesis. It cannot be said: it is included under accident; because we say: it is not a highest genus for what is under it from the categories because it is not essential for them. He said in Sharh al-Maqasid: The meaning of substance is the soul of a thing and its reality, so it is essential, unlike accident, for accident means what occurs to the subject. The occurrence of a thing to another is only after the realization of its reality, so it is not essential for the individuals under it, though it may be essential for the portions in them, like 'walking' for its reality which occurs to animals, end. And in al-Dawwani: The point is a real type, not a relative type. As for the first, because its individuals agree in reality. As for the second, because it does not fall under any of the categories. Even if it falls under accident, but accident is not a genus for what is under it. Or because it is simple, i.e., it is not composed of genus and differentia, so it is not a relative type due to the necessity of relative type being included under genus. Both aspects are weak. As for the first, because it does not indicate that it has no genus, but rather that it has no highest genus. Perhaps it has a specific genus, because what is confined to the categories are only the highest genera, so it is possible that it is composed of mental parts united in external existence, like other essences composed of genera and differentiae. As for the second, because mental simplicity is denied, and external simplicity does not benefit, because the genus is not an external part; rather it is a mental part. So it is possible that the point has a mental part which is its genus.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage critically examines the logical definition of the point (nuqta) and the claim that it is simple (basita). The main text states that 'they are simple' is contradicted by the definition as 'end of line'. Dasuqi clarifies that the contradiction means if they were not simple, that would violate the assumption of simplicity. He then distinguishes external simplicity (unchallenged) from intellectual simplicity (problematic) because the point as end of line is conceptually composite: it is composed of 'end' and its restriction to a line. Attar presents a syllogism: if the point had a genus, it would not be simple; but it has no genus; therefore it is simple. However, he critiques this: the point might fall under accident, but accident is not a highest genus because it is not essential to its subordinates. Citing al-Dawwani, he argues the point is a real type (naw' haqiqi) not a relative type (naw' idafi), because its individuals agree in reality and it does not fall under any category. Two arguments for it being a real type are presented and both are shown weak. The first argument only proves no highest genus, not no genus at all; it might have a specific genus. The second argument claiming mental simplicity is denied because the genus is a mental part, so the point can have a mental genus even if no external one. The discussion illustrates the logical rigor in determining whether a concept is simple or composite, using the point as a test case.

Key Terms
نقطة
بسيطة
جنس
نوع حقيقي
نوع إضافي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, what is the main critique of al-Dawwani's claim that the point is a real type (naw' haqiqi)?
A) It has no genus at all.
B) It has no highest genus, but may have a specific genus.
C) It is an accident.
D) It is composed of genus and differentia.

Key Takeaway
Logical analysis of simplicity requires distinguishing external composition from intellectual composition; a concept can be ontologically simple yet conceptually composite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. In a kalam debate on divine simplicity, a mutakallim argues: 'If God had distinct attributes, He would be composite. But He is simple, so He has no attributes.' Reconstruct this as a conditional syllogism and identify whether it commits the fallacy of equivocation on 'simple' (external vs intellectual).
?
2. Analyse the definition of 'hadd' (penalty) in usul al-fiqh: 'Hadd is a specified punishment for a specified sin.' Is this a real definition (hadd haqiqi) or a description (rasm)? Use the criteria of genus and differentia.

The Philosophers' Definition of the Point and Natural vs. Mathematical Entities
Author explains natural vs. mathematical lines, surfaces, and bodies, and the status of the point.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to (1) identify the real definition (hadd haqiqi) versus descriptive definition (rasm) of the point, and (2) distinguish between natural and mathematical lines, surfaces, and bodies in the philosophical framework.

Core Idea
The point is an accident, not a substance; its real definition is 'a thing having position, not divisible at all.'

This passage presents the philosophers' view on the point, clarifying that it is not a substance but an accident inhering in a natural line. It also distinguishes natural (substantial) entities from mathematical (accidental) ones. Understanding this distinction is crucial for later discussions of metaphysics and geometry in Islamic philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of the point in the main text
Read the opening line: 'Know that the point in the terminology of the philosophers is an expression for the end of the line.' Note that this is a descriptive definition (rasm), not a real definition (hadd haqiqi).
The main text gives a simple identification, not a full logical definition.
2
Find Dasuqi's clarification that it is not a real definition
In the commentary, Dasuqi states: 'His saying: “an expression for the end of the line” is not a real definition of the point.' This signals that a more precise definition is needed.
3
Extract the real definition from Attar's gloss
Attar provides the real definition: 'a thing having position, not divisible at all.' Identify the genus (thing having position) and differentia (not divisible).
The real definition captures the essence: it is an indivisible positioned entity.
4
Understand the natural vs. mathematical distinction
Trace the pairs: natural line (substance) vs. mathematical line (accident), natural surface vs. mathematical surface, natural body vs. mathematical body. Note that natural entities are hylomorphic compounds; mathematical entities are accidents inhering in them.
The point is the endpoint of a mathematical line, hence also an accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعْلَمْ أَنَّ النَّقطة في اصطلاح الحكماء عبارة عن نهاية الخط
الدسوقي
(قَوْلُهُ: وَاعلَمُ . . . إلخ) حاصلُهُ أنَّ الحكماء يقولون : إنَّ ما قبل القسمة طولاً ؛ يُقالُ لهُ : خطّ طبيعي، وهو مُركَّب من الهيولى والصُّورة؛ لَا مِنَ الجواهر الفردة ؛ لاستحالة وجودِهَا عندَهُم ، والامتداد القائم بذلك الخط الطَّبيعي القابل للقسمة في جهةِ الطُّولِ؛ يُقال له : خطّ تعليمي، ونهايته النقطة، فكلُّ مِنَ الخطّ التَّعليمي، والنقطة عندَهُم : عَرَض . وإذا وُضِعَ خط طبيعي بجانبِ آخَرَ ؛ بحيثُ صارًا قابلين للقسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً ؛ كان الحاصل منهما : سطح طبيعي (١) ، والامتداد القائم به القابل للقسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً ؛ يُقالُ لَهُ : سطح تعليمي، ونهايته : خط تعليمي .
(۱)
وإذا وُضِعَ سطح طبيعي فوقَ آخَر ؛ كان الحاصل جسماً طبيعيًّا، والامتداد القائمُ بِهِ القابلُ لِلقسمة طولاً وعَرْضاً وعمقاً يُقالُ لَهُ : جسم تعليمي، ونهايتُهُ السَّطح، فتحصَّلَ مِن قولِنَا : إنَّ الخطوط والشطوحَ والأجسامَ الطَّبيعيَّة جواهر قائمةٌ بِنَفْسِهَا، مُركَّبَةٌ مِنَ الهيولى والصُّورة عندَهُم ، وأنَّ النُّقطة والخطوط والشطوحَ
العطار
المتقدّمونَ ، ومِنهُمُ الشَّيخُ في الشّفاء ؛ فعندَهُمْ أنَّ النِّسبة بينهما : العموم والخصوص المطلق، وأنَّ الإضافي أعمُّ مُطلقاً مِنَ الحقيقي، واحتجوا عليهِ بأَنَّ كُلَّ حَقيقي؛ مندرج تحت مقولةٍ مِنَ المقولاتِ العَشْرِ ؛ لانحصار الممكنات فيها، فكلُّ نوع حقيقي حينئذ له جنس ؛ لكنَّهُ غيرُ تامّ لِجواز وجودِ نوع بسيط لا جنس له بناءً على جواز تركب الماهِيَّةِ مِن أَمرَيْنِ مُتساويَيْنِ؛ تَأَمَّلْ (قَوْلُهُ : عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ نِهَايَةِ الْخَطِّ ليسَ تَعريفاً حقيقيًّا للنقطة، وتعريفها الحقيقي؛ أنَّها شيءٌ ذو وضع لا يقبل القسمة أصلاً، واستيفاء الكلام على النقطة في حواشينا على شرح القاضي ؛ زاده على متن أشكالِ التَّأسيس في عِلْمِ الهندسة .
(۱) (قَوْلُهُ : سطح طبيعي) الصواب نصبهما على الخبرية لـ «كان» ولا يصح جعلهما اسماً لها مؤخّراً إذا لا يخبر بالمعرفة عن النكرة، بل العكس.
Know that the point in the terminology of the philosophers is an expression for the end of the line. Dasuqi: (His saying: 'Know... etc.') Its summary is that the philosophers say: That which is before lengthwise division is called a natural line, and it is composed of matter and form, not of individual atoms, due to the impossibility of their existence according to them. The extension subsisting in that natural line, divisible in length, is called a mathematical line, and its endpoint is the point. So both the mathematical line and the point are accidents according to them. If a natural line is placed alongside another such that they become divisible in length and breadth, the result from them is a natural surface (1), and the extension subsisting in it divisible in length and breadth is called a mathematical surface, and its endpoint is a mathematical line. If a natural surface is placed above another, the result is a natural body, and the extension subsisting in it divisible in length, breadth, and depth is called a mathematical body, and its endpoint is the surface. Thus it is established from our statement that natural lines, surfaces, and bodies are substances subsisting by themselves, composed of matter and form according to them, and that the point, mathematical lines, surfaces... Attar: The early philosophers, among them the Shaykh in al-Shifa', held that the relationship between them is absolute universality and particularity, and that the relative is absolutely more universal than the real. They argued for this by saying every real type is included under one of the ten categories, because possible things are confined to them. So every real type then has a genus; but it is incomplete because of the possibility of a simple type having no genus, based on the possibility of the essence composed of two equal things. Ponder. (His saying: 'an expression for the end of the line' is not a real definition of the point. Its real definition is: a thing having position, not divisible at all. The complete discussion of the point is in our glosses on the commentary of al-Qadi, added to the text of Ashkal al-Ta'sis in geometry.) (1) (His saying: 'natural surface') The correct is to put them both as predicate of 'kana', and it is not valid to make them its delayed noun, as one does not predicate a definite of an indefinite, rather the opposite.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage defines the point in philosophical terminology and explains the distinction between natural and mathematical entities. The main text states that the point is 'the end of the line'. Dasuqi's commentary elaborates: natural line is a substance composed of matter and form (hylomorphic), not of atoms. The mathematical line is the extension (accident) that subsists in it, and the point is the endpoint of that mathematical line. Both are accidents. Similarly, natural surfaces and bodies are compounds of matter and form, while mathematical surfaces and bodies are accidents inhering in them. The endpoint of a mathematical surface is a mathematical line; the endpoint of a mathematical body is a surface. The natural entities are substances; the mathematical entities are accidents. The footnote corrects a grammatical point in the phrase 'سطح طبيعي' as predicate of 'كان'. Attar's commentary returns to the earlier debate about the relationship between real and relative universality, citing the early philosophers (including Ibn Sina) who held that the relative is absolutely more general than the real, arguing that every real type falls under a category and hence has a genus. However, the argument is deemed incomplete because a simple type with no genus is possible. The passage ends by noting that the definition of the point is a descriptive definition (rasm), not a real definition; the real definition is 'a thing having position, not divisible at all'.

خط تعليمي

عرض

Three Opinions on the Nature of the Point
The commentator enumerates three distinct views on the ontological status of the point.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three ontological views on the point (nuqta) as presented in this passage.

Core Idea
Three schools debate whether the point is a real substance, a mental construct, or a quality.

In this passage, the commentator al-‘Attar explores the nature of the point (nuqta), which is used as an example in logical discussions. He presents three distinct positions on its ontological status. Understanding these views is essential for correctly interpreting logical examples and for appreciating how philosophers classify entities within the Aristotelian categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
Extract the three opinions from the Arabic: first, that the point is a simple existent not under any category; second, that it is a mental affair (amr i‘tibari); third, that it falls under the genus of quality.
Look for the phrases: الأول, الثاني, الثالث.
2
Understand the key terms
Note the terms: نوع حقيقي (real kind), أمر اعتباري (mental affair), كيف (quality). These reflect different ontological commitments.
3
Examine the implications for exemplification
The commentator states that the exemplification by the point is only valid if it is a complete real kind. This shows the practical consequence of the ontological debate for logical examples.
4
Analyze the third opinion in detail
The third opinion divides quality into four kinds by induction: psychological, sensible, qualities of quantities, and dispositional. The point is placed under qualities of quantities, as per the Shaykh's Commentaries.
The inductive division is claimed to be exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثمَّ التَّمْثِيلُ بِالنُّقْطَةِ إنَّما يصح إذا كانتِ النُّقطة تمام النوع الحقيقي. فيها مَذاهب ثلاثة : الأَوَّلُ : أَنَّها نَوعٌ مَوجودٌ بسيط لم يندرج تحت مقولة، وَصِحَةُ التَّمثيل مبنيَّةٌ عليه؛ لَا عَلَى أَنَّهَا مِنَ الأمورِ الاعتباريَّةِ كَمَا في الحاشية، فإنَّهُ سَهْو. الثَّاني : أنَّها أمر اعتباريُّ. الثَّالثُ : أَنَّها داخلةٌ تحتَ جنسِ الكَيْفِ، وحصرُ الكيف في أقسامِهِ الأربعةِ، وَهِيَ الكيفيات النَّفسانيَّةُ والكَيفيَّاتُ المحسوسة وكَيفيَّاتُ الكَمِّيَّاتِ والكيفيات الاستعداديَّة؛ استقرائي، فَهِيَ واردةٌ على الحصر، على أنَّ مير زاهد نقل أَنَّ الشَّيخَ صرَّحَ في التَّعليقاتِ بِأَنَّ النُّقطةَ كَيفيَّةٌ في الخطّ كَالتَّربيع. فتكون داخلةٌ تحت قسم الكيفيات المختصة بالكميَّاتِ.
Then the exemplification by the point is only valid if the point is the complete real kind. Concerning it there are three schools: First: that it is a simple existent kind not falling under a category, and the soundness of the exemplification is based on this, not on its being among mental affairs as in the marginal note, for that is an oversight. Second: that it is a mental affair. Third: that it falls under the genus of quality, and the encompassment of quality in its four divisions—namely psychological qualities, sensible qualities, qualities of quantities, and dispositional qualities—is inductive, so they are restrictive, and that Mir Zahid reported that the Shaykh stated in the Commentaries that the point is a quality in the line like quadrature. Thus it falls under the division of qualities specific to quantities.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe by the commentator al-‘Attar explaining three opinions on the nature of the point (nuqta) that were invoked in the exemplification of a previous argument. The commentator begins by stating that the exemplification by the point is only valid if the point is understood as a complete real kind (al-naw‘ al-haqiqi). He then enumerates three distinct positions. The first opinion holds that the point is a simple existent kind (naw‘ mawjud basit) that does not fall under any of the ten Aristotelian categories. On this view, the exemplification is sound because the point is a real entity, not a mental construct. The second opinion considers the point to be a mental affair (amr i‘tibari), meaning it has no external existence but is only conceptually posited. The third opinion places the point under the genus of quality (kayf). The commentator notes that the fourfold division of quality (into psychological, sensible, quantities, and dispositional) is reached by induction (istiqra‘i), so these four are exhaustive. He then quotes Mir Zahid’s report that the Shaykh (presumably Ibn Sina or another philosopher) stated in his Commentaries that the point is a quality in the line, similar to quadrature, thus falling under qualities specific to quantities. The commentary thus clarifies that the three opinions are not arbitrary but represent real differences in ontology, each affecting the validity of using the point as an example.

نقطة
نوع حقيقي
أمر اعتباري
كيف

Key Takeaway

The Differentia as Not Entirely Shared
Commentary on condition for a part to be a differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a differentia from a genus by checking whether the part is entirely shared with other quiddities.

Core Idea
A differentia is a part that is not entirely shared—otherwise it would be a genus.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies the condition for a part (juz') to serve as a differentia (fasl). The key is that the part must not be the entirety of what is shared (tamm al-mushtarak). If it were entirely shared, it would be a genus, not a differentia. Understanding this is essential for correctly classifying the five universals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the part (juz') in a quiddity
The passage discusses a part that is shared between the quiddity and another type, like 'growing' shared between plants and animals. Locate this part in the definition.
2
Check if it is entirely shared
Determine whether this part is the entirety of what is shared (tamm al-mushtarak). If it is, it is a genus; if not, it may be a differentia.
The passage emphasizes that the differentia is not the entirety of what is shared, nor a part of that entirety.
3
Consider simple quiddities
Simple quiddities have no parts, so a part cannot be shared with them. This ensures that even a partially shared part distinguishes from simples, making it a differentia.
4
Apply the test to an example
Take an example from fiqh or kalam and classify a property as genus or differentia based on whether it is entirely shared.
For instance, 'living being' is entirely shared among animals, so it is a genus. 'Rationality' is not entirely shared (only humans), so it is a differentia.

فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التصورات أو كانَ مُشتركاً بين الماهية ونوع آخَرَ كالنَّامي. لكن لا يكون تمام المشترك، فهذا الجزء لا يمكن أن يكون مشتركاً بين الماهية وجميعِ ما عدَاهَا، إذْ مِنَ الماهيَّاتِ ما تكون بسيطةً لا جزء لها. ولذلك قال بعضُهم: وعلى هذا؛ فَالفصل هو الذي يميّز الماهية في الجملةِ، وَلَا يكون تمام المشترك بينها وبين غيرها، ولا جزءه، ولا يرد الجنس؛ لأنَّه تمام المشترك، وَلَا مثل الجوهرِ النَّاطق؛ لأنَّ الكلام في الأجزاء المفردة . (قَوْلُهُ : مَا تَكُوْنُ) أي : ماهيَّة تكون بسيطة . (قَوْلُهُ : إِذْ مِنَ المَاهِيَّاتِ مَا تَكُونُ بَسِيْطَةٌ) المرادُ أنَّ ذلك الأمر لازم على كُلِّ حال فالتَّمييزُ عَن الماهية البسيطة لا يتخلفُ، وليس المرادُ أنَّه لا يكونُ مُميَّزاً إلا والحاصل أنَّ هذا الفصل مُمَيَّزُ عَمَّا شارَكَهُ في الوجودِ كالماهيات البسيطة الَّتي لا جنس لها قطعاً، ثمَّ قد يكونُ مُميَّزاً عَمَّا شاركَهُ في الجنس إن كان هناك إِنْ ذلكَ، وَوُجود الماهية البسيطة مُحقَّق، فإنَّ المركَّبَ لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَنتهي بالتحليل إلى البسيط؛ لأنَّ كُلَّ كَثرةٍ وإِنْ كانَت غير مُتناهيةٍ؛ لا بُدَّ لَهَا مِنَ الوَاحِدِ لأَنَّهُ مَبدؤُهَا، فلو انتفى الواحد؛ انتفى الكثير لانتفاءِ مَبدئِهِ ولِذَا قالَ فِى التَّجريد: وجود البسيط والمركَبِ معلوم بالضَّرورة . ا.هـ. واعلم أنَّ ما ذكرَهُ الشَّارِحُ هُنَا مَأخوذُ مِن كلامٍ السَّيِّدِ في حاشية القطب، فإِنَّهُ قُدِّسَ سِرُّهُ بعدَ أنْ ناقش دليل الشارح القطب واعترضه؛ قال: وهذا الاعتراضُ مِمَّا لَا مدفعَ لَهُ إلَّا إذا ثبتَ أَنَّهُ لا يجوز أَنْ يكونَ لماهيَّةٍ واحدةٍ جِنسان لا يكونُ أحدُهُمَا جزءاً لِلآخَرِ، ولم يثبتْ هَهُنَا؛ أي: في حصر جزء الماهية في الجنسِ والفصلِ، فَلَا بُدَّ مِن تَرْكِ هذا الدَّليلِ والتَّمَسُّكِ بِدَليل آخَرَ وهو أنْ يُقالَ: جزءُ الماهية إذا لم يكن تمام المشترك بينها وبين نوع مَا مِنَ الأنواع المباينةِ لَهَا؛ فإمَّا أَنْ لا يكونَ مُشتركاً أصلاً بينها وبين نوع مُبَايِّنِ لَهَا؛ فيكونُ فَصْلاً للماهِيَّةِ مُميّزاً لَهَا عَن جميع المباينات، وأمَّا أنْ يكونَ مُشتركاً بينَها وبين غيرها؛ لكن لا يكون تمام المشترك بينها، فهذا الجزء لا يمكنُ أنْ يكونَ مشتركاً بين الماهية وبينَ جميعِ ما عداها؛ إذْ مِن جملة الماهياتِ ماهيّة بسيطة لا جزء لَهَا، فيكون هذا الجزء مُميّزاً للماهيَّةِ عَنِ الماهيَّاتِ الَّتي لا تُشارِكُها في هذا الجزء؛ فيكونُ فَصْلاً للماهية ا.هـ.
Chapter: On the foundations of concepts. Or it (the part) is shared between the quiddity and another type, like al-nami (growing). But it is not the entirety of what is shared. So this part cannot be shared between the quiddity and everything other than it, because among quiddities there are simple ones with no parts. Therefore some said: On this basis, the differentia is that which distinguishes the quiddity in general, and is not the entirety of what is shared between it and others, nor a part of it. Genus is excluded because it is the entirety of what is shared. The example of 'rational animal' is excluded because we are speaking of single parts. (His statement: 'what is' means a simple quiddity. (His statement: 'since among quiddities there is a simple one') The intent is that this matter is necessary in every case; distinguishing from a simple quiddity is never absent, not that it distinguishes only that. The upshot is that this differentia distinguishes from what it shares existence with, like simple quiddities that have no genus absolutely. Then it may also distinguish from what it shares genus with, if there is that. The existence of simple quiddity is verified, for a composite must, by analysis, end in a simple; because every multiplicity, even if infinite, must have a unity as its origin; if the one is absent, the many are absent due to the absence of its origin. For this reason it is said in al-Tajrid: The existence of the simple and composite is known necessarily. End. Know that what the commentator mentioned here is taken from the words of al-Sayyid in his gloss on al-Qutb; for he, sanctified his secret, after discussing and objecting to the argument of the commentator al-Qutb, said: This objection has no repulsion unless it is established that one quiddity cannot have two genera where neither is part of the other, and that is not established here—that is, in restricting the part of the quiddity to genus and differentia. So it is necessary to abandon this argument and hold to another argument: that is to say: the part of the quiddity, if it is not the entirety of what is shared between it and some type that is disparate from it, then either it is not shared at all between it and any disparate type—in which case it is a differentia for the quiddity, distinguishing it from all disparates—or it is shared between it and others but not the entirety of what is shared. This part cannot be shared between the quiddity and everything other than it, since among quiddities there is a simple quiddity with no part. So this part would distinguish the quiddity from quiddities that do not share this part; thus it is a differentia for the quiddity. End.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of differentia (fasl) and the conditions for a part of a quiddity to serve as a differentia. The text begins by stating the chapter on the foundations of concepts. It considers the case where a part (juz') of the quiddity is shared with another type, like 'growing' (al-nami) shared between plants and animals. The key condition is that this part must not be the entirety of what is shared (tamm al-mushtarak) between the quiddity and others. If it were the entirety, it would be a genus. The commentator explains that such a part cannot be shared with everything other than the quiddity, because there exist simple quiddities with no parts at all. Hence, this part necessarily distinguishes the quiddity from those simple quiddities. The commentator then cites an opinion: the differentia distinguishes the quiddity in general, and is neither the entirety of the shared nor a part of that entirety. Genus is excluded because it is the entirety of the shared. The example 'rational animal' is excluded because the discussion concerns single parts (like 'rational' alone), not compound definitions. The passage then elaborates on simple quiddities: a composite must ultimately reduce to simples by analysis, because every multiplicity requires a unity as its origin. This is a necessary truth. Finally, the commentator notes that the discussion is taken from al-Sayyid's gloss on al-Qutb. Al-Sayyid had criticized al-Qutb's argument and proposed an alternative: a part that is not entirely shared may still be a differentia if, when it is not shared at all with any disparate type, it distinguishes from all disparates; or if it is partially shared, it cannot be shared with everything (due to simple quiddities), so it distinguishes from those lacking it, thus serving as a differentia.

Key Terms
فصل
تمام المشترك
جزء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for a part (juz') to be a differentia (fasl)?
A) It must be entirely shared with all other quiddities.
B) It must not be the entirety of what is shared between the quiddity and others.
C) It must be a simple part with no further composition.
D) It must be shared only with simple quiddities.

Key Takeaway
A differentia is a part that distinguishes the quiddity but is not the entirety of what is shared; otherwise it would be a genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify which of the following parts is a genus and which is a differentia: 'living being' (hayy) for 'human', and 'rational' for 'human'. Explain using the condition of not being entirely shared.
?
Consider the 'illa of 'intoxication' in the prohibition of wine. Is 'intoxication' a differentia? Check if it is entirely shared with other intoxicants like beer.

What Is Mantiq?
advanced
10 min
Why Simple Quiddities Guarantee the Differentia Condition
Argument that a part cannot be shared with simple quiddities, establishing differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the argument that a part shared between quiddities cannot be shared with simple quiddities, thereby guaranteeing its role as a differentia.

Core Idea
Simple quiddities lack parts, so any part of a composite quiddity must distinguish from them.

This passage presents a crucial argument: a part of a quiddity, even if shared with some types, cannot be shared with simple quiddities because simples have no parts. Since composites reduce to simples by analysis, and simples exist necessarily, any such part must be a differentia. This argument resolves the puzzle of a partially shared part and shows why the differentia condition (not being entirely shared) is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Establish the existence of simple quiddities
The passage states that among quiddities there are simple ones with no parts. This is known necessarily, as composites reduce to simples and multiplicity requires unity.
Cite the principle from al-Tajrid: 'The existence of the simple and composite is known necessarily.'
2
Consider a part that is shared but not entirely
Take a part of a composite quiddity that is shared with another type, like 'growing' shared between plants and animals, but not entirely shared.
3
Show it cannot be shared with simple quiddities
Simple quiddities have no parts, so they cannot share any part. Therefore, this part is absent from simple quiddities.
This is a logical deduction from the definition of simple.
4
Conclude it is a differentia
Since the part distinguishes the composite quiddity from simple quiddities (and possibly from other composites lacking it), it qualifies as a differentia.
The two-case approach in al-Sayyid's alternative argument: if not shared at all, it distinguishes from all disparates; if partially shared, it still distinguishes from simples.

What Is Mantiq?

Defining Necessary Accident (Lazim) and Its Scope
Author defines lazim and then commentary debates its scope regarding personal necessary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the definition of lazim (necessary accident) in Islamic logic and identify why it must include personal necessary properties.

Core Idea
A complete definition of 'necessary accident' must cover both essence-bound and individual-bound inseparable properties.

In this lesson, we examine the definition of 'lazim' (the necessary accident) from the Tadhheeb al-Mantiq. The author gives a concise definition: that which cannot be separated from the thing. But a careful reading reveals a subtler point: does 'thing' refer only to the essence (mahiyya) or also to individual entities? The commentary tradition debates this very question, refining the definition to ensure it includes necessary properties of individuals, like the blackness of a particular Ethiopian. By working through this passage, you will learn to parse a logical definition and assess its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and definiens
Locate the term being defined (al-lazim) and the defining phrase: 'in imtana'a infikakuhu 'ani al-shay' (if its separation from the thing is impossible). Mark these clearly.
2
Recognize the three causes of impossibility
The commentators note that the impossibility of separation can be due to the essence of the subject (e.g., evenness of four), the essence of the necessary itself, or an external cause (e.g., blackness for an Ethiopian). List each with an example.
3
Notice the change from 'essence' to 'thing'
The author deliberately used 'shay' (thing) instead of 'mahiyya' (essence). Reflect on why this change was made: it avoids certain problems related to division of universals.
4
Pinpoint the critique by al-Muhashi
Al-Muhashi argues that if 'thing' means only essence, then the definition excludes lazim al-shakhs (individual necessary), such as a specific blackness for an Ethiopian. Explain why this would be a problem for comprehensiveness.
5
Follow the resolution by al-Sayyid
Al-Sayyid clarifies that 'thing' should be interpreted broadly to include both essence and individual, thus including lazim al-shakhs. Confirm that the definition is now comprehensive.

فَصْلٌ: في مبادئ التَّصورات [اللَّازِمُ]: (إِنِ امْتَنَعَ انْفِكَاكُهُ)؛ أي: انفكاكُ كلّ واحدٍ من الخاصَّةِ والعَرَضِ العام (عَنِ الشَّيْء؛ فَلَازِمٌ). الدسوقي العطار (قَوْلُهُ : إِنِ امْتَنَعَ انْفِكَاكُهُ... إلخ) أي: لا يجوز أن يفارقه، وإِنْ وُجِدَ في غيره ؛ فَلَا يردُ اللازم الأعم، وذلك الامتناعُ إمَّا لِذاتِ الملزومِ أو لِذاتِ اللَّازِمِ أو لِأَمْرِ مُنفصل كَالسَّوادِ لِلحبشي؛ قاله عبد الحكيم. انفكاكه (قَوْلُهُ : عَنِ الشَّيْءِ) عدل عن تعريف اللازمِ بِمَا يمتنعُ انفكاكه عن الماهية لِعَدَم ما يقتضيه في كلامِهِ، وَهُوَ تَقسيمُ الكُلّيّ بالنَّظَرِ لِلماهية، ووجودُ مَا يُنافيه ؛ وهو خروج لازم الوجودِ، ولزومُ تَقسيم الشَّيء إلى نفْسِهِ ومُباينِهِ في قولِهِ؛ بالنَّظر إلى الماهية أو الوجودِ، لكنَّهُ لزمَهُ أَنَّ التَّقسيم غيرُ حاصرٍ؛ إذْ لا يَنحصرُ مَا يمتنعُ عَنِ الشَّيء في لازم الماهية ولازم الوجودِ ؛ لأنَّ كليهما لازم بالقياس إلى الماهية، فيخرج لازمُ الشَّخصِ مِنْ حيثُ إِنَّهُ لازمُ الشَّخصِ عَنِ التَّقسيمِ؛ قالَهُ المحشّي، وتعقبه البعضُ بِمَنْعِ عدم الاقتضاء، والسَّند قول المصنّف : وهو الخارج عن الماهية ... إلخ، وأنَّ لازم الشَّخص خارج عَنِ الشَّيء؛ لأنَّ المرادَ بِهِ الماهيَّةُ ؛ بدليل قولهِ السَّابق : الخارج عَنِ الماهِيَّةِ ؛ على أنَّ لازمَ الشَّخص داخل في لازم الوجودِ وراجع إليهِ؛ لِكَونِهِ لازماً للماهيَّةِ مِنْ حيثُ خصوص أحد الوجودين ا.هـ. وهو ناشئ مِنْ قِلَّةِ التَّدبرِ ، أَمَّا الأَوَّلُ ؛ فَلِأَنَّ قولَ المحشّي : وهو تقسيم ... إلخ؛ بيانُ لِلمقتضى، وأمَّا تقدُّمُ أنَّ الخاصَّةَ والعرض العام؛ كُلَّ منهما خارج عَنِ الماهِيَّةِ ؛ فَشيءٌ آخَرُ ، وأمَّا الثَّاني؛ فقد قالَ السَّيِّدُ في حاشية المطالع : إذا عرفت اللَّازِمَ بِمَا يمتنع انفكاكُهُ عَنِ الشَّيء؛ لم ينحصر في لازم الماهية ولازم الوجود، فإِنَّ اللَّازِمَ مُطلقاً ما يمتنع انفكاكُهُ عَنِ الشَّيء الذي نُسِبَ إليهِ؛ سواءٌ كَانَ كُلِّيًّا أو جزئيا .ا.هـ. فهذا صريح في أنَّ المراد بالشَّيء ما يشمل الماهية وغيرها، فيرد حينئذ
Chapter: On the Principles of Conceptualizations. [Al-Lazim]: (If its separation is impossible) i.e., the separation of each of al-khassa and al-'arad al-'amm (from the thing; then it is necessary). al-Dasuqi and al-'Attar: (His saying: if its separation is impossible... etc.) i.e., it is not permissible for it to leave it, even if it is found in something else; so the more general necessary is not excluded. And that impossibility is either due to the essence of the subject, or due to the essence of the necessary, or due to an external cause like blackness for the Ethiopian; said by 'Abd al-Hakim. Its separation: (His saying: from the thing) He deviated from defining al-lazim as that whose separation from the essence is impossible because of what it requires in his speech, and it is the division of the universal with respect to the essence, and the existence of what contradicts it; which is the exclusion of al-lazim al-wujud, and the necessity of dividing the thing into itself and its opposite in his saying: with respect to essence or existence. But it follows from him that the division is not exhaustive; since what is impossible to separate from the thing is not limited to lazim al-mahiyya and lazim al-wujud; because both are necessary with respect to the essence, so lazim al-shakhs (personal necessary) is excluded from the division; said by al-Muhashi. And someone followed him by denying the lack of implication, and the basis is the author's statement: it is external to the essence ... etc., and that lazim al-shakhs is external to the thing; because what is meant by it is the essence; as evidenced by his previous statement: external to the essence; and that lazim al-shakhs is included in lazim al-wujud and reverts to it; because it is necessary for the essence in terms of the particularity of one of the two existences. End. And it arises from lack of reflection. As for the first; for the statement of al-Muhashi: it is a division ... etc.; is an explanation of the implication. As for the precedence that al-khassa and al-'arad al-'amm are both external to the essence; that is another matter. As for the second; al-Sayyid said in Hashiyat al-Matali': If you define lazim as that whose separation from the thing is impossible, it is not limited to lazim al-mahiyya and lazim al-wujud, for lazim absolutely is what cannot be separated from the thing to which it is attributed, whether it is universal or particular. End. This is explicit that what is meant by 'thing' includes essence and other than essence. So then it applies.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and critical discussion of the concept of 'necessary accident' (lazim). It opens a new chapter on the principles of conceptualizations. The definition given is: 'If its separation from the thing is impossible, then it is necessary.' The commentators explain that this means it cannot leave the subject, even if it exists in other subjects as well; thus, the more general necessary (like animality for man) is not excluded by being found in others. The impossibility can be due to the essence of the subject (e.g., the evenness of four), or due to the essence of the necessary (e.g., the separability of something), or due to an external cause (e.g., blackness for an Ethiopian, which is accidental but inseparable due to climate). The text then notes that the author deliberately changed the definition from 'impossible to separate from the essence' to 'impossible to separate from the thing' to avoid certain problems. However, a critic (al-Muhashi) points out that if 'thing' is taken to mean 'essence', then the division into lazim al-mahiyya and lazim al-wujud is not exhaustive because it excludes lazim al-shakhs (individual necessary), i.e., properties that are necessary for a particular individual but not for the essence. For example, the specific blackness of a particular Ethiopian is necessary for that individual but not for the essence of humanity. The critic argues that this must be included. Then another commentator (al-Sayyid in Hashiyat al-Matali') clarifies that the word 'thing' in the definition should be taken broadly to include both essence and individual, so that lazim al-shakhs is included. Thus, the definition is comprehensive. The passage ends with the statement that the definition as given covers all necessary accidents, including personal ones. The critical refinement here is that the definition must be interpreted correctly to avoid an incomplete division.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what problem does al-Muhashi identify in the definition of lazim if 'thing' is interpreted as 'essence'?
A) It makes the definition circular.
B) It excludes necessary properties of individuals (lazim al-shakhs).
C) It includes too many properties.
D) It confuses essence and accident.

Key Takeaway
A complete definition of necessary accident must cover inseparable properties of both essences and individuals.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the property of 'laughter' for a human. Determine whether it is a lazim of the essence of humanity or a personal necessary for a specific human. Use the three-criteria classification (essence-bound, existence-bound, external cause).
?
Al-Sayyid argues that the word 'thing' in the definition of lazim includes both essence and individual. Find a real example from Islamic theology or jurisprudence where distinguishing personal necessary from essential necessary changes a ruling.
