The Naming of the Absolute Proposition
Commentary on the naming of the absolute proposition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the reason the absolute proposition is called 'absolute' and explain the metaphorical naming (majaz mursal) involved, while recognizing the counterarguments regarding custom and language.

Core Idea
The absolute proposition is named after the actuality of the relation it signifies, but this naming is controversial.

This passage explains why a proposition that judges with the actuality of the relation between subject and predicate is called 'absolute' (mutlaqa). The commentators argue that the actuality is understood from the proposition, so the signified (the relation) is named after the signifier (the proposition). However, objections arise because custom and language do not always imply actuality, as in universal affirmative statements. The discussion involves a type of figurative speech (majaz mursal) and debates about inversion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim about the naming
Find the statement that the absolute proposition is named because the actuality of the relation is understood from it. Note that this is described as naming the signified by the name of the signifier.
2
Recognize the objections
Al-Dusuqi and al-Shaykh Yasin object that it is not necessary for a proposition without modality to imply actuality; custom and language do not understand actuality from statements like 'Every human is an animal'.
The example 'Every fire is cold' is problematic but used to show possibility.
3
Distinguish the levels of understanding
Al-Attar restricts the understanding to custom and language, but al-Isam objects that this contradicts the earlier rule for negative absolute propositions. A possible solution is that the understanding is based on the word itself, disregarding custom.
This shows the complexity of the issue.
4
Analyze the metaphorical naming
The passage explains that the uttered proposition is used for the conceptual one (majaz mursal). Alternatively, there is an inversion: 'absolute' primarily refers to the relation, so the proposition is named after it metaphorically.
Consider the two possibilities: naming the signified by the signifier, or the signifier by the signified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يُفهم منها فعليَّةُ النّسبةِ، فسُمِّيَتِ القضيَّةُ الَّتي حُكم فيها بفعليَّةِ النِّسبةِ مطلقة؛ تسمية للمدلول بِاسْمِ الدَّالّ .
الدسوقي
.
والحاصلُ : أَنَّهُ ليسَ بِلازم أنْ يكونَ مَعنى القضيَّةِ إذا لم تذكرِ الجهةُ أنَّ النِّسبةَ ثابتة بالفعل؛ لجواز أنْ يكونَ ثُبوت المحمول للموضوع على سبيل الإمكان، كَقولِكَ : كلَّ نارٍ باردةٌ . وفي الشيخ ياسين مَا :نصُّهُ : (قولُهُ: لأنَّ القضيَّةَ إِذا أُطلِقَتْ ... إلخ) فيه : أنَّ هذا لا يصحُ كُلِّيًّا؛ إذ لا يفهم العرفُ واللُّغةُ مِن مثل قولنا : «كل إنسان حيوان»، وزيدٌ قائمٌ أَوْ يقومُ» فعليَّة النِّسبة .
العطار
(قَوْلُهُ: يُفْهَمُ مِنْهَا فِعْلِيَّةُ النِّسْبَةِ) أي: بحسب العُرفِ واللُّغةِ كَمَا فَيَّدَ بذلك المصنِّفُ وغيرُه ، ونظر فيه العصامُ بأَنَّهُ يُنافي ما سبقَ مِن أنَّ العُرْفَ يُفهَمُ مِنَ القضيَّةِ السَّالبة إذا أطلقت الدَّوامَ الوصفي، إلا أنْ يُقالَ (۱): يُفهم معناها نظراً إلى نفس اللَّفْظِ معَ قطع النَّظرِ عَنِ العُرْفِ، وفي المحشّي : فيهِ أنَّ هذا لا يصحُ كُليًّا؛ إذ لا يُفهمُ العرفُ وَاللُّغةُ مِن مثل قولِنَا : كُلُّ إنسان حيوان وزيدٌ قائم فعليَّة النّسبة ا.هـ وقد يُجابُ : بأنَّ هذا توجية لِلتّسمية في الجملة؛ أي: يُفهم ذلك في الجملة ولو في بعض الأفراد.
(قَوْلُهُ : تَسْمِيَةٌ لِلمَدْلُوْلِ بِاسْم الدَّالّ لأنَّ القضيَّةَ الملفوظة إذا لم تُقيَّد بجهةٍ ؛ يُعلَمُ منها فعليَّةُ النِّسبةِ، فلمَّا كان هذا المعنى مفهوماً مِنَ القضيَّة الملفوظة سُمِّيت المعقولة بها، فيكونُ مَجازاً مُرسلاً مِن قَبيلِ تَسمية المدلول باسم دالّهِ، فَقولُ الشّارحِ : سُمّيت القضيَّةُ ؛ أي: المعقولةُ، كَذَا عَلَّلَ، وفيه قصورٌ، فَمِنَ ثُمَّ قيل: في العبارة قلبٌ ; لأنَّ المطلقة اسم للنّسبة المدلولة للقضيَّة، فسُمِّيَتِ القضيَّةُ الدَّالّة على النسبةِ بلفظ مُطلقة مجازاً مِن قبيل تسميةِ الدَّالّ باسم المدلول .
(۱) (قولُ العطَّارِ : أَنْ يُقالَ مُحرَّفةٌ بحذفِ كلمة فَالمناسبِ أنْ يُقالَ كَمَا لَا يَحْفَى، ثمَّ إِنَّ عِبارةً الشَّارحِ خاليةٌ مِنَ التَّقييد بالعرفِ واللُّغةِ والتَّقييد بذلك في شرح القطبِ فَلَا
العصام ا.هـ. الشَّرنوبي.
یرد تنظیر
It is understood from it the actuality of the relation, so the proposition in which judgment is made with the actuality of the relation is called absolute; naming the signified by the name of the signifier. Al-Dusuqi: The conclusion: that it is not necessary that the meaning of the proposition when the modality is not mentioned is that the relation is actually established; because it is permissible that the affirmation of the predicate to the subject be in the way of possibility, like your saying: 'Every fire is cold.' And in al-Shaykh Yasin: his text: (His saying: because the proposition when it is absolute... etc.) in it: that this is not universally valid; for custom and language do not understand from examples like our saying: 'Every human is an animal', and 'Zayd is standing or stands' the actuality of the relation. Al-Attar: (His saying: It is understood from it the actuality of the relation) i.e., according to custom and language, as the author and others restricted it thus. And al-Isam objected to it that it contradicts what preceded, that custom understands from the negative proposition when absolute the descriptive perpetuity, unless it is said (1): its meaning is understood considering the word itself, disregarding custom. And in al-Muhashshi: in it: that this is not universally valid; for custom and language do not understand from examples like our saying: 'Every human is an animal' and 'Zayd is standing' the actuality of the relation. End quote. And it may be answered: that this is a justification for the naming in general; i.e., it is understood in general, even if only in some individuals. (His saying: Naming the signified by the name of the signifier) Because the uttered proposition, when not qualified by a modality, is known from it the actuality of the relation. So when this meaning was understood from the uttered proposition, the conceptual proposition was named by it. So it is a figurative expression (majaz mursal) of the type of naming the signified by the name of its signifier. So the commentator's saying: 'the proposition was named'; i.e., the conceptual one. Thus he justified, but it has deficiency. Hence it was said: in the expression there is inversion; because 'absolute' is a name for the relation signified by the proposition, so the proposition indicating the relation was named with the word 'absolute' metaphorically from the type of naming the signifier by the name of the signified. (1) (Al-Attar's saying: 'that it may be said' is distorted by omission of a word, so the appropriate is that it be said as is not hidden. Then the commentator's expression is free from restriction by custom and language, and the restriction in that in the explanation of al-Qutb, so no objection occurs. Al-Isam end quote. Al-Sharnubi.
Source pages p. 568

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that explains why the proposition that judges with the actuality of the relation is called 'absolute' (mutlaqa). The commentators engage in a debate about whether this naming is always accurate. The passage begins by stating that the absolute proposition implies the actuality of the relation, hence it is named after that meaning—a case of naming the signified by the signifier. Al-Dusuqi then objects, arguing that it is not necessary for a proposition without mention of modality to imply actuality, because it could be possible, as in 'Every fire is cold' (which is impossible but used as an example of possibility?). He cites al-Shaykh Yasin's point that custom and language do not understand actuality from such statements. Al-Attar then explains that the understanding of actuality is according to custom and language, but al-Isam objects that this contradicts the earlier statement that the negative absolute proposition implies descriptive perpetuity (perpetuity of the predicate throughout the subject's existence). A possible reconciliation is that the understanding is based on the word itself disregarding custom. The discussion continues with the point that the naming is metaphorical: the uttered proposition is used for the conceptual one, or there is an inversion where the signifier is named after the signified. The passage clarifies that the term 'absolute' primarily refers to the relation, not the proposition itself.

Key Terms
المطلقة
الجهة
النسبة
المجاز المرسل

Key Takeaway
The absolute proposition is named for the actuality of the relation it indicates, but this naming is controversial and involves metaphorical language and inversions.
